Free Talk

World Anecdotes 87

— Sea Traveler

Snowdon is the highest peak in England and Wales, measuring 3,571 feet. The original name means "Snow Mountain."

In the lifeboat teams along the coast of Sweden, each team must have one female crew member.

The salaries of soldiers in the U.S. Army and Navy are the highest of any country in the world, which shows the country's wealth.

The current national trend in the United Kingdom is to drink more tea and less beer. Most doctors do not agree, believing that the drawbacks are even deeper, as tea is even more harmful than beer.

The Lord Mayor of London is extremely busy with social engagements, often participating in one or two banquets every night, at least 400 times a year.

The most popular novelist in all of Europe is British Charles Dickens. His novels have been printed and published a total of 25 million copies.

The famous German national anthem was composed in 1841 by August Heinrich Hoffmann von Fallersleben, a German residing in Heligoland (then a British territory). The original manuscript recently appeared at an auction and fetched only three pounds and thirteen shillings.

A Record of Staying at Wujian 88

— Xiaodie

I, Xiaodie, have often visited the eighteen flower docks of Liuxia Wujian. This spring, Monk Xingyuan of Xiaohe Mountain invited me to stay at Jinlian Temple. Those joining us were Mu Huai and Yu Kun. Xiaohe Mountain is eighteen miles from Liuxia, with secluded streams and valleys. The bamboo paths and stone steps are spotless. Further in are the Yucen and Tongwu areas of the Wu Dynasty, considered the most beautiful parts of Liuxia Wujian. However, it rained that day, and we heard there were tigers in Tongwu, so we couldn't explore everything. In the fourth lunar month, Yu Kun returned to Dongyue. I followed Mu Huai to stay at Xixi. That night, the moonlight was very bright. We walked by moonlight from Xixi Bridge, past Daxiaolongju Dock, to Dongyue, only about seven miles. The mountain flowers had already faded, and early fireflies flickered in the grass like solitary stars. Late bamboo shoots pushed through the stones, sometimes hindering our feet, while the murmuring streams were always beside us, though unseen. Yu Kun loved to sing, and he sat barefoot on the stone bridge with two or three good friends, singing in the clear moonlight. Hearing footsteps, they abruptly stopped, and called out to each other with laughter through the bamboo fence, the moonlight shadows completely shattered. Yu Kun said, "Why not take advantage of the moonlight to climb to the top of North Peak and chant?" But Mu Huai declined, saying his feet were tired, and thought it better to save that enjoyment for tomorrow, when we would climb Shiren Ridge and return to West Lake via Tianzhu. I gazed at North Peak, the misty moonlight vague and indistinct, imagining tomorrow's journey. That night, I was so excited I couldn't sleep. On the ninth day, three bamboo sedan chairs set off from Liuxia, going south along Xixi. Gradually, we entered a bamboo path. Two peaks, like snail shells, stood proudly outside the bamboo forest, called Jinzhu Ridge. The foot of the ridge was somewhat winding, with bamboo forests rising high, while above and below were the east and west Mu Docks, secluded and beautiful, still retaining the charm of the flower docks. After passing Jinzhu Ridge, the stone steps became steeper, and the mountain scenery also changed. The lush green beauty was mixed with majestic and rugged features. Were these the clouds of heaven, or the stones of the mountain? Shaking my clothes, I felt like I wanted to fly away on the wind. A hundred layers of emerald screens stood upright in front, seemingly hundreds of feet high. The wind blew the leaves, making rustling sounds, like a qin or a zither, with a lingering melody, unlike any worldly sound. Mu Huai said, "Behind the mountain is Shiren Ridge, where West Lake can be seen like an inkstone pond. The mountains above the lake are not without beauty, just like officials who carefully groom their appearance, while only the peaks of Liuxia are unadorned and unpretentious. For hundreds of years, they have been rarely visited and seldom praised, so their natural purity has not been carved. It's a shame." He continued, "Mountains are like people. Those who are famous lose their purity. We have found this secluded secret. Perhaps it's best not to tell outsiders." Now, the two of you are far away in northern Anhui, constantly thinking of our past travels, which are difficult to repeat. I have hastily written this record. Will Yu Kun and Mu Huai think I am being too talkative?

A Polish Stork 89

— Gengxin

Near Staro Gard Gdański, Poland, there is a small town with a long-abandoned distillery. A stork built its nest on top of it. The air was clear, which the stork enjoyed. Recently, workers climbed to the top to renovate the building and resume operations. This stork temporarily perched on a nearby lemon tree, but the new home was not to its liking. Soon, it returned to its old home. The next day, the workers came again, and the stork moved again. This happened back and forth for a week. Finally, the worker was defeated by the stork's patience, so he let it be. Today, this stork still lives atop the distillery's chimney, spending its life in swirling smoke. Its feathers have turned completely black, making it look almost like a huge crow from afar.

New Tales of Seedlings 90

— Ke Ding'an

The area around the Huangpu River is vast, with densely packed shops and markets. The so-called residential areas are also overflowing, making it difficult to find a place to live. In recent years, commerce has declined and unemployment is rampant. When these people were employed, they sometimes struggled to make ends meet. Once they are laid off, they have nothing to eat and wait anxiously. How can they survive? Some of the stronger ones turn to theft to get what they want, while the weaker ones beg for help to stay alive. Regardless of whether they are strong or weak, or whether they steal or beg, the cause is unemployment. If everyone could live and work in peace and have peace of mind, then social stability would be guaranteed. Look at Japan. At night, they can sleep soundly with only paper windows covering their doors. Why can't we be like them? It is truly regrettable. What I am about to describe is what I have personally witnessed. I will tell my friends about it. My friends say that Shanghai has such gangs. They don't necessarily have to be unemployed to do this. I think Shanghai is so big that there is nothing strange about it. I will describe it to readers as a precaution.

One day, I was visiting a friend and passed through Mongolia Road. A man, poorly dressed, was holding a glass bottle in his right hand and a piece of white paper. He was supporting his left leg with his left hand and walking with difficulty. However, he was not focused on walking and was looking around with his eyes, acting in a pretentious manner. I was curious and wanted to see what was going on, so I followed him. When we arrived near the vegetable market, a man, who looked to be about fifty years old and who seemed to be visiting Shanghai from the countryside for the first time, came towards us. While he was looking around, the first man suddenly bumped into him, and the glass bottle shattered with a crash. The second man was startled by the sudden sound, and the first man grabbed his collar, crying out, "I came from the hospital. The medicine in the glass bottle was just bought from the pharmacy. I have a doctor's prescription here." As he spoke, he took out the white paper from his right hand and showed it to the second man. He continued to cry, "I am a laborer. I only earn three or four dimes a day. It was really difficult for me to spend a dollar to buy this medicine." The second man argued that he didn't bump into him, but the first man said, "Is there any reason to intentionally bump into someone holding a glass bottle of medicine to make it break?" The two men argued for a long time. A bystander, acting as a peacemaker, said, "Just pay him four dimes to settle the matter." The second man reluctantly took out the money and gave it to the first man, who then left angrily. Looking at the white paper he had thrown away, it was an old prescription, and the medicine in the bottle was obviously tap water.

Last Thursday, I was walking from my residence and passed Baoshan Road. A child was walking ahead of me, carrying a lacquered bucket slowly, as if expecting something. I was about fifty paces away from him when a flashy rickshaw suddenly came along at Yokohama Bridge. A young woman was sitting in the rickshaw with several books on her lap, probably a student at Patriotic or Yanzhe School. At this time, the child seemed to have reached his destination and rushed forward, colliding with the rickshaw puller. The bucket fell and the people fell. The red lacquer flowed all over the street. The child got up and cried, grabbing the rickshaw puller's clothes and crying, "This lacquer was entrusted to me by my master to deliver to a certain place. It cost more than two dollars. Pay me quickly, pay me quickly." He continued to cry. Many people gathered around to watch, and everyone thought that because he was young, he must not be lying. Finally, the young woman took out a dollar and waved him away. The so-called lacquer was just a bucket of red mud. The child was probably an expert in this field.

A Grand Gathering of the First Elegant Gathering of the Songshan Thatched Cottage Painting Collection 91

— Daya

Mr. Feng Chaoran of Wujin is famous throughout the country and is currently known as Gu Lu. He uses the pseudonym Songshan Jushi and named his studio Songshan Thatched Cottage. His students are numerous and talented. Recently, to connect friendships and hone their artistic skills, they organized the first elegant gathering of the Songshan Thatched Cottage Painting Collection on the Buddha's Birthday in the fourth lunar month at the residence of Mr. Wang Boyuan in West Shanghai. Around 3:00 p.m., more than twenty teachers and students took a group photo. The host also brought out rare ancient and modern masterpieces to share with the guests. While admiring them, Mr. Chaoran gave earnest instructions, truly a great teacher of his time. In the evening, the students gathered for a banquet to celebrate Mr. Chaoran's birthday. Mr. Chaoran looked at them and was happy. During the banquet, guest Mr. Mu Ouchu gave a congratulatory speech, and the host performed magic tricks to entertain the guests. The students who attended that day were Sun Qionghua, Zhou Shujuan, Zhang Yanhua, Zheng Qihua, Mao Guihua, Shen Xiuhua, Xi Jinhua, Xie Yaohua, Yu Yinghua, Li Dehua, Tang Hua and other ladies, as well as Xing Mingsheng, Zhang Gunian, Yuan Anpu, Cao Junjian, Zhang Yayong, Zheng Mukang, Lu Yanshao, Cheng Xiaoguang, Wu Digang and other gentlemen. Guests included Mr. Mu Ouchu, Wu Hufan, Xie Shengzu, Zhu Qiting, Zhu Jingbo, Li Zunyong and other gentlemen. I am also a private student of Mr. Chaoran, so I was fortunate enough to participate in this grand gathering, and I am recording the magnificence of the moment.

Around the Yellow Sea (19) 92

— Huang Yanpei

Some Japanese Shinmura projects have also failed in trials. Bihai is a successful experimental farming village.

On April 18th, I took a train from Tokyo to Anjo Prefecture. Shimo-Anjo is a town name belonging to the village of Hekikai-gun, Aichi Prefecture.

I got off the train in the faint morning light and had a meal. The landlady came out to greet the guests. An opportunity to talk had arrived. Hekikai is famous for its cooperative businesses. They call cooperation "Kumiai."

I asked, "Your Kumiai is very developed. The signboard says 'Japanese-Western Kumiai Dining Hall.' I guess it's also a Kumiai. What exactly is the meaning of Kumiai? What are the benefits of being a member?" She replied, "Being a member of the Kumiai means you can discuss things. You can participate in meetings. There are also very enjoyable group trips. Recently, we went to Tokyo to see the cherry blossoms. It only cost each person 1.50 yuan." I asked, "Are there any other benefits?" She took the dishes inside, stopped for a moment, and then came out and said, "Other restaurants can call geishas, but our dining hall is not allowed to call geishas. There are more than a hundred geishas in Anjo."

Numerous bicycles passed by outside the door, mostly female students, but also male students, aged between fourteen or fifteen and seventeen or eighteen.

I entered the Hekikai-gun Purchasing and Sales Kumiai Federation. Director Tsuruta came out to meet me and answered my questions in great detail. Their Kumiai stipulates four types: (1) Purchasing Kumiai, (2) Sales Kumiai, (3) Credit Kumiai (i.e., lending Kumiai), and (4) Utilization Kumiai, which is a method of using publicly equipped machinery.

The main items sold by their Sales Kumiai are food and eggs.

We then visited their agricultural association, town hall, agricultural supplementary school, agricultural and forestry school, poultry breeding and incubation Kumiai, Fukugama utilization factory, Aichi Prefecture Agricultural Experiment Station, and finally visited a farm owned by the Itakura family.

Looking at the town hall, the entire town's budget book was detailed, standardized, and explained meticulously and executed rigorously. From the lowest level, I could see their scientific spirit.

Entering the agricultural supplementary school, they recruit ordinary elementary school graduates for a three-year course. The male students take agricultural courses, and the female students take domestic science and sewing courses. After graduation, they serve in rural villages or homes. Countless bicycles were parked inside the door. I realized that the numerous students I had just seen cycling to the countryside were students from this school. I guessed that the families of the students in this school all had considerable wealth and could afford bicycles. I also guessed that the students in this school were scattered in various villages and the area was relatively large, so they needed bicycles. So I asked the principal, "Are the families of the students in your school all of middle-class wealth or above?" He replied, "Yes, agricultural laborers cannot afford to enter this school." I asked, "What do they do after graduation?" He replied, "Ninety-nine percent become agricultural managers, and only one percent become laborers." I asked, "What percentage of laborers in this town are property owners?" He replied, "Sixty percent are owner-farmers, twenty percent are tenant-farmers (i.e., those who farm on land owned by others), and twenty percent are owner-tenant-farmers." Looking at it this way, it can be considered good, but the education and economy of the rural villages have not yet reached the area of my ideals.

The Rotary Club of Su Bu.

The Future World (5) 93

— Tianxu Wosheng

If one could concentrate one's mind and have it be the master, then wherever one thought, one could surely reach. That would be like a god. One must abandon one's physical body to be good. The Lao Mountain Taoist in the "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio" was a person who had achieved spiritual liberation. When his disciple was on the mountain with him, his master would certainly put his physical body somewhere else and only use his spirit to instruct him. That is why he was able to pass through walls without hindrance. It was not using the method in "Goose Illusions Compiled," using loadstone to burn smoke and create a false wall. When his disciple ran home with his physical body, he could not leave his form and even tried to think of passing through walls with his physical body, and he broke his head. So I think the people of the future world will all be ghosts, ghosts talking to ghosts, or people who are close to ghosts talking to ghosts. They will surely be able to shake hands and talk heart-to-heart, just like humans in the present world. However, ghosts still have to die and become Jiang. Their level will advance further, seemingly like the golden shrimp becoming a tadpole. It is like sperm turning into a person, and tadpoles turning into mosquitoes. From human death to becoming a ghost, and mosquito death to transforming into what? Because humans' eyesight is limited, we only see the physical bodies of mosquitoes. How do we know that mosquito ghosts are not in another world, becoming mosquito Jiang? No one has ever talked about what Jiang die into. However, I say that the spirit is immortal and will surely exist forever in the world, for thousands of autumns and myriads of ages without perishing. Therefore, Confucius was able to dream of the Duke of Zhou. In reality, how was it a dream? How do we know that he was not clearly seeing the Jiang of the Duke of Zhou? If the people of the world could make their dream souls have a master, going east when they wanted to go east and going west when they wanted to go west, like Confucius dreaming of the Duke of Zhou, dreaming when he wanted to dream and seeing the Duke of Zhou when he wanted to see him, then Confucius would surely be extremely strong in spirit. After his decline, he did not have this ability, so he could not dream of the Duke of Zhou again. If Confucius had long abandoned his physical body and specialized in working with the Duke of Zhou in his dreams, he would not have aged. Why would he have troubled himself with a carriage and two horses on a dusty road? When he wanted to dream, he could dream; when he wanted to see him, he could see him. This shows that his dream soul was already able to be independent. If he abandoned his physical body, he would not need carriages and horses to travel to various countries. With a single thought, he would arrive at a certain place. It would also be very easy for him to practice his art of governing the country and bringing peace to the world. He would only need to use his telepathic powers to guide the minds of the people of the world, and they would be like the compass needles that have passed through magnetism, and they would definitely not have different directions. I say that even if the people of the future world graduate from telepathy specialized schools, if they do not abandon their physical bodies, I am afraid that it will not be thorough. My future world is the spiritual world, which is also the world of gods. Because there are no physical bodies, there is no pain. Isn't it as happy as a god? In the future, when you come to this future world, you will surely abandon your physical body, but your relatives will surely mistakenly think that you are dead and will inevitably cry a lot, causing you to secretly laugh. (The End)

A Glimpse of the Idleness of Foreign Silk 98

The weather is not good, and the silk production is not abundant.

According to previous years, at this time, the demand for silk for foreign countries was constant. The revitalization of the market was also a major event in the whole year. Therefore, the demand for foreign silk is not strong. Furthermore, the replacement of current silver by banknotes is also a major reason.

Yarn and Cotton Yarn Sales to Sichuan Merchants Are Strongest 100

The yarn market, which has been brewing for a long time, is gradually showing signs of life. This is mainly because the demand for current yarn in the northern region is unusually strong, and locally produced yarn accounts for the majority. This area used to be dominated by Japanese yarn, but now, due to unfavorable exchange rates, the price of yarn in Shanghai is relatively low, so there is a constant stream of purchases. The volume of yarn entering Sichuan is also strong, and the situation for other merchant groups is also improving. As a result, market sentiment is excited, and the market is rising. However, most sellers are bearish, because the coarse yarn market is stagnant and the overall situation is still unstable, so there are still those who short the market when it rises. However, comparing the overall situation, the market price in Shanghai is lower. The price of 20-count Palace Maid yarn in Qingdao and other places is 196 taels, and the price of 16-count Five Star yarn is 180 taels. Therefore, merchants from the northern routes are constantly trading and purchasing in Shanghai. If the business of various merchant groups can continue uninterrupted, the inventory can be greatly reduced. Furthermore, recently, many factories have switched to spinning finer yarn, so in the future, there may inevitably be a period of sharp price increases. However, the chaotic political situation is a fly in the ointment.

Human Bids See Increases of One to Two Taels. At the exchange, the opening price for human bids in the morning market was higher due to good current sales and tight market conditions, with each bid rising by four, five, six, or seven cents. In the afternoon, it was heard that current yarn business was picking up in various regions, and some were rushing to cover short positions, with each bid rising by one tael, two, four, or five cents. The total transaction volume for the day was 36,600 bales. It was found that Gongtai sold 1,300 bales, Ruidai 1,200 bales, Senkang 1,050 bales, and Yichang 1,450 bales. Dafeng bought 1,450 bales, Tianlong 1,050 bales, Gengfeng 1,750 bales, Yidai 1,500 bales, and Xiesheng 1,100 bales. The closing prices for human bids are recorded below:

Grain and Rice Market Downstream is Active and Tending to be Firm 104

Few Ships Arriving, Tightness Reported at Production Origin

Zhabei: Yesterday, the Xinzha rice market showed an upward trend. There were a large number of people visiting the market early in the morning, and buyers took advantage of this opportunity to add to their inventories. Thick japonica rice with fresh top-grade goods rose by 30 cents, and the sales of thin indica rice from Ningbo were active. The road for hair rice was also good, and the price increased by about 20 cents. The road for early rice in the local city and villages was extremely smooth, and the price also increased by several cents. Ocean Du tips and Yin glutinous rice were firm. Few ships arrived on the inside route, and few were loaded with customer tips, so the market rose. Production origin market shouted for tightness, so the price of various goods was difficult to weaken.

South Shanghai: Yesterday, there were slightly fewer merchant groups arriving in Shanghai from the South Shanghai area. There was a lack of connection for thin indica rice, and sporadic movements of about five or six hundred stones. The top-grade market price was firm, and the middle level shouted for an increase of 20 cents. Although japonica rice from Changshu, Wuxi, northern Jiangsu, and Suzhou and Tongzhou was received, the number was small. Local shop transactions were more active, so the trend was up two or three cents. Ocean Du tips each kept their original market price, and the port tips lacked goods and had no market change. Yin yuan had no glory. It is estimated that there were more than ten numbers of buckets of river undergrain from Changshu, Wuxi, Yixing, Tongli, Pinghu, Qingpu, and Liantang, opening a market of 1,600 to 1,700 dan.

Newly Arrived Foreign Rice Already Sold 105

Orders Will Soon Arrive in Force, Prices will Gradually Decrease

Yesterday, the customer indica rice was sold smoothly in this street, and the market was lively. However, a new ship of foreign rice already pre-ordered, the Saigon rice number 12, had just arrived. The appetite in this street was also good, but because the orders were about to arrive in force, the cargo owners were very willing to sell quickly, so the market was flat and soft. Yesterday, Wanxing handled the sale of 20 packs of Deputy Number One Saigon rice at a price of 11.5 yuan. High-number one etc. have not yet been sold.

Flour Market Returned to Flatness in the Afternoon 106

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market was quite excited in each month at the beginning, because the price of foreign wheat was only two or three cents lower. However, the weather was bad and there were thunderstorms, so the highest price in this month and July reached 1 tael, 1 cent, and 5.5 mills. Then, as the weather cleared up, many bulls from the inland merchants took the opportunity to come back, so the market returned to softness. When the market opened in the afternoon, it was still stable at first, but then the trend was very flat because the buying interest was low, and the transactions in each market were sparse. The recent term was slightly softer than in the morning, and the distant term was still stable. November was the first time it was opened for bidding, and there were few transactions. The price once opened to 2 taels, 2 cents, and 0.25 mills in the afternoon, and the closing price was also slightly softer. As a result, this month was 2.5 mills higher than the previous day's closing price, July was 5 mills higher, August was 7 mills higher, September was 1 cent higher, October was 1.5 cents higher, and November was unchanged.

Wheat Market Initially Strong, Then Settled 107

The market in the futures wheat market yesterday morning and afternoon showed a trend of first being strong and then settling. In the morning, because the weather was bad, the market sentiment was up, and the highest price in each month was better than the previous month by three, four, or five cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, because the flour market turned flat and the weather cleared up, the inland market sentiment and merchants all turned flat and relaxed. The recent term was slightly lower than in the morning by one or two cents, and the distant term hovered. November was the first time it was opened for bidding, and the highest price in the morning was 4 taels, 3 cents, and 9 mills. In the afternoon, it gradually fell, falling about seven or eight cents from the highest price. The new wheat harvest is widespread in the south of the Yangtze River, and it will probably be fully harvested in about ten days, so the weather conditions thereafter are very important to the rise and fall of the market. As a result, this month was 2 cents higher than the previous day, July and August were 2 cents higher, September was 3 cents higher, and October was 2 cents higher.

Silk and Tea: Xinchang Cocoon Market Ends 109

Each Business's Receipt Decreased by 70%. Cocoon Price at 46 Yuan. This year's silkworm season in the four villages of Xinchang was not good. The early silkworms were all abandoned, and the late silkworm cocoons were only about 30%. Less than ten cocoon businesses opened for weighing, and the amount received by each business in the ten-plus days of weighing was 70% less than in previous years, and the quality of the cocoons was poor. The cocoon market ended, and the cocoon businesses have all stopped weighing. The highest cocoon price was 54-55 yuan, the lowest was 41-42 yuan, and the average was 46 yuan. The cocoon type received by each business this year was all of the zero-baking nature. Only four silk merchants rented factories and weighed cocoons.

Qimen Tea Plummeted by More Than 20 Taels 110

Yesterday, the tea market of foreign companies in this port saw the Qimen black tea from the second and third merchant groups such as Yingzhuang, Qiahe, and Tianyu tending to be less active in their intake, and the recognized prices were stricter than before. The total transaction volume of black tea in the city reached more than 1,600 boxes. The top market price opened at 205 taels, a sharp drop of more than 20 taels from last week. The market for Zhenmei green tea was not significant yesterday. The Tunxi Zhenmei that arrived a few days ago has not yet been officially priced. However, Pingshui pearl tea was actively being searched for by Tianxiang, Jinlong, Yihe, and Xiehe, and almost no goods remained in stock. The price also increased by four or five taels.

Celebrating the Promulgation of the Provisional Constitution

The 9th District Party Headquarters held a grand meeting in Longhua to celebrate the promulgation of the Provisional Constitution and the second anniversary of the Premier's burial. Wu Tiecheng's Conversation 113

Hoping that the Guangdong Incident Can be Turned from Danger to Safety

This reporter met with Central Committee member Wu Tiecheng at Wanglu yesterday and asked him when he would return to Beijing and how far the negotiations on the peaceful resolution of the Guangdong Incident had progressed. Wu said that he had originally planned to return to Beijing as soon as possible, but because he had been away from Shanghai for a long time last time, there were still many private matters to be dealt with, and he could also take this opportunity to rest for a few days. As for the Guangdong Incident, we always hope to turn danger into safety and avoid another war. Although Mr. Zhang Puquan has been sent to Guangdong by the Central Government to negotiate, the results are still unknown. It is said that Mr. Zhang has now left Guangdong and is returning north. I will wait for Mr. Zhang to arrive in Shanghai before returning to Beijing together.

China-Germany Radio

Officially Announced Yesterday 114

400 Free Reports Issued

China-Japan Communication Awaits Ministry Order

According to the Far East News Agency, the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications has achieved good results since the commencement of the China-Germany trial telegraph. Therefore, it was specially announced yesterday that the China-Germany telegraph has been officially opened. Four hundred free tickets were pre-printed for Chinese and foreign merchants to collect as a souvenir. The following is a record of the information obtained yesterday:

Demand for Free Reports Exceeds Supply: The radio station specially prepared 400 free report tickets as a souvenir for the official opening of the China-Germany telegraph and to promote it widely. These tickets were freely available to Chinese and foreign merchants for one day of free telegram transmission. As of 11:00 AM yesterday, all the tickets had been claimed. Those who arrived later continued to arrive in an endless stream. The format of the ticket is recorded below. The ticket is white with blue characters, with both Chinese and English versions. The top of the ticket is printed with the words "Ministry of Communications International Radio Station Free Report Ticket." Below it is divided into: (1) No fee will be charged for sending reports with this ticket; (2) The number of words is limited to 25; (3) The destination is all parts of Germany; (4) Valid until June 1, 20; (5) Receiving location: Sassoon Building, 1 Renji Road.

Telegram Types, Number of Words, and Prices: Telegrams sent from China to all parts of Germany are divided into three types. The first is express telegram, which costs 3.45 yuan per word and can reach its destination in about 20 minutes. The second is slow telegram, which costs 1.13 yuan per word and can reach its destination in about 1 hour. The third is daily news telegram, which costs 1.15 yuan per word, but is limited to a minimum of 25 words and will reach its destination in 48 hours.

No More Free China-France Communications: China and France have already officially opened telegraph communications, and the results are very good, but there has been no free opening. The station intends to officially conduct a free day as a promotion. The above information was sent to the French radio station to solicit opinions (according to the free regulations, both parties must agree; otherwise, our side will not charge a fee, but the other side will still charge a fee). Later, the French side replied that the radio station had already been free for one day during the China-France trial telegraph in mid-December last year. Therefore, there will be no more free China-France communications.

China-Japan Communication Has Not Received Ministry Order: According to a staff member of the radio station speaking to a reporter from the Far East News Agency, the unofficial China-Japan telegraph communication has already begun. It was originally intended to hold the official China-Japan telegraph communication at the same time as the China-Germany telegraph today (i.e., yesterday). However, because the Ministry of Communications has not yet issued an order for the official China-Japan telegraph communication, it cannot be realized within the next few days. It will be necessary to wait for the Ministry order to arrive before a date can be set.

U.S. Congressional Delegation Arrives in Shanghai 115

Studying the Problem of Restoring Silver Prices

Pittman May Arrive This Morning as Well

Mr. Oddie (Photo by Qiao Shanfu) 116

Those who greeted him included Mr. An Lide, the U.S. Commercial Counselor in China, and others. U.S. Senator Pittman is taking the President Jefferson via Japan to Shanghai and may arrive this morning as well. The entire congressional delegation is scheduled to enter Beijing in mid-month and depart Shanghai for home on the 18th of this month. Mr. An Lide is scheduled to host the congressional delegation at the U.S. Commercial Counselor's Office at 3 Guangdong Road at 4:00 PM this afternoon and invite Chinese and foreign bankers to meet and talk.

Mr. Robinson (Photo by Qiao Shanfu) 117

Delegation Members and Itinerary: The congressional delegation that departed from the United States to China this time consists of five people in total. Senator Oddie, the Republican representative from Nevada, is currently staying at the Cathay Hotel. Senator Robinson, the Democratic representative from Arkansas, is staying at the residence of U.S. Consul General Cunningham. Congressman Doughton, the Republican representative from Iowa, is

Mr. Gisborn (Photo by Qiao Shanfu) 118

Staying at the residence of U.S. Assessor Bandi. Congressman Gisborn, the Republican representative from Vermont, is staying at the Cathay Hotel. Senator Pittman, who is arriving in Shanghai this morning, is the Democratic representative from Nevada. Nevada is a famous silver-producing region in the United States. Mr. Pittman is the chairman of the U.S. Senate Silver Committee, and Mr. Oddie is the chairman of the Mining Committee. Both of them have proposed bills in the U.S. Senate to rescue silver prices and

Mr. Doughton (Photo by Qiao Shanfu) 119

Supported the Chinese silver loan matter, making their names widely known. Regarding the itinerary of the congressional delegation, Messrs. Oddie and Pittman will stay in Shanghai temporarily, while Messrs. Robinson, Doughton, and Gisborn are scheduled to take the Nagasaki Maru to Japan tomorrow and stay there for a week. The congressional delegation will return to Shanghai on the 12th of this month and then jointly enter Beijing on a scheduled date. They will depart Shanghai on the Tingte Shenghao transport ship on the 18th of this month and return to their home country via Manila.

Important Tasks in China: This reporter specially visited Mr. Oddie at the Cathay Hotel yesterday to discuss the silver price issue. Mr. Oddie declared that they are scheduled to stay in China for eighteen days on this trip, and their only task is to investigate and study the silver issue and do not intend to make any suggestions for the time being. They have established a temporary office in the Cathay Hotel and invited Chinese and foreign bankers to exchange opinions. The purchasing power of hundreds of millions of people in the East has been greatly affected due to the disastrous fall in silver prices, causing a decline in world commerce. Therefore, in order to restore the original prosperity of world commerce, it is necessary to catch up quickly and fix the silver price. He and Mr. Pittman are indeed representatives of the silver-producing region, but the countries that supply silver to the world include Mexico and England and France, and Nevada in the United States is only a small part of it. His secondary mission for this trip is to rescue the silver mines in Nevada. The recovery of silver prices depends on the cooperation of the countries concerned. It may be beneficial to convene an international silver conference and work together. The reporter then asked whether the United States was willing to be the initiator of the conference. Mr. Oddie replied that he doubted it very much. As for the silver loan issue, which was once very noisy, it is now silent. Whether the congressional delegation will raise the old issue again this time has not been discussed by both parties.

Five Types of Public Bonds Drawn Yesterday 120

Total Principal Repaid: Silver $8,250,000

The Ministry of Finance's Public Debt Department held a lottery for five types of public bonds at 2:00 PM yesterday in the Hong Kong Road Bankers' Association meeting hall. The details are recorded below:

Attendees: The representatives who attended yesterday included Zheng Lai, Director of the Public Debt Department; Shen Zaochi from the Audit Yuan; Dai Hongquan from the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court; Sun Xingyan and Li Tisheng from the Central Bank; Chen Wenzhao from the Bank of China; Pei Yunqing from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Yan Junan from the Money Trade; Zheng Huanlan from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce; and over forty guests.

Lottery Procedure: (1) Ringing the bell to open the meeting; (2) Reading the will respectfully; (3) Report by the Director of the Public Debt Department; (4) Moment of silence; (5) Inspecting the lottery sticks and registers; (6) Conducting the lottery; (7) Announcing the winning numbers; (8) Adjourning the meeting.

Amount of Public Bonds: The total amount of the five types of public bonds drawn this time is as follows: (1) The 6% Public Bond of the Republic of China, Year 7 (1918), with a total issuance of $45,000,000, began repayment in Year 17 (1928) in 20 installments over 10 years. Six installments have already been repaid. This is the seventh installment, with five bonds drawn for a principal repayment of $2,250,000. (2) The Military Supply Public Bond of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, issued in Year 17 (1928), with a total amount of $10,000,000. Starting from Year 18 (1929), the principal is repaid twice annually, each time repaying one-twentieth of the total amount. Four installments have already been repaid. This is the fifth installment, with five bonds drawn for a principal repayment of $500,000. (3) The Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bond of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government was also issued in Year 17 (1928), with a total amount of $40,000,000. Starting from the second half of Year 17, it is repaid in 10 installments over 5 years. Five installments have already been repaid. This is the sixth installment, with ten bonds drawn for a principal repayment of $4,000,000. (4) The Disaster Relief Public Bond of Year 18 (1929), with a total issuance of $10,000,000. Starting from June of Year 18, the principal is repaid twice annually, each time repaying one-twentieth of the total amount. Four installments have already been repaid. This is the fifth installment, with five bonds drawn for a principal repayment of $500,000. (5) The Customs Revenue Public Bond of Year 19 (1930), with a total issuance of $20,000,000. Starting from June of Year 19, the principal is repaid twice annually, each time repaying one-twentieth of the total amount. Two installments have already been repaid. This is the third installment, with five bonds drawn for a principal repayment of $1,000,000. All the winning bonds mentioned above are scheduled to begin payment on June 30th. The principal of all winning bonds, along with the interest due on the bonds, will be paid jointly by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications.

Winning Numbers: (1) The winning numbers for the 6% Public Bond of the Republic of China, Year 7, are 9, 34, 54, 67, and 98. (2) The winning numbers for the Military Supply Public Bond are 10, 19, 30, 32, and 49. (3) The winning numbers for the Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bond are 8, 12, 26, 35, 46, 51, 65, 76, 87, and 91. (4) The winning numbers for the Disaster Relief Public Bond of Year 18 are 13, 28, 73, and 84. (5) The winning numbers for the Customs Revenue Public Bond of Year 19 are 19, 55, 15, 73, and 92. The total principal to be repaid for the five types of public bonds above is $8,250,000.

The Yat Sen Warship Held a Flag-Raising Ceremony Yesterday 121

Returning to the Fleet in One Week

The newly completed Yat Sen warship of the Navy held a flag-raising and oath-taking ceremony at Gaochang Temple Wharf yesterday. Chen Jiliang, Commander of the First Fleet, presided over the ceremony. At 10:00 AM, the ceremony was conducted as scheduled. Captain Chen Hongtai took the oath and raised the flag. Chen Jiliang then presented the seal and delivered a speech, the gist of which was that the Chinese Navy had not completed a single warship in decades. Now, the Ministry of Navy had completed five warships amidst very difficult economic circumstances, the Yat Sen being one of them. Although our naval strength cannot be compared to that of Europe and America, the strength of naval power does not depend on the size of the warships but on the efforts and good training of the personnel. During the outbreak of the European War, the German warship Emden had a displacement of only 3,000 tons, not much different from our Yat Sen, but its power and its exploits are well known to everyone. Although it was eventually sunk, its great achievements remain among the Germans to this day. Therefore, in the future, everyone must strive for strength in terms of knowledge, academics, and training, and not judge naval strength solely based on the size of the warships. The ceremony ended at noon, and the warship is currently docked in Shanghai harbor and will sail to the capital to rejoin the fleet in a week.

Lao Jingxiu and others

The Enthusiasm for the June 3rd Memorial Preparation 124

This year's June 3rd Opium Suppression Memorial has been jointly planned by the Shanghai Special City Party Department, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the China National Anti-Opium Association. Details of the various measures have already been reported. It is now learned that the memorial's preparatory committee believes that the commemoration should be enthusiastically held at a time when domestic opium suppression is lax and the International Conference on the Limitation of Dangerous Drugs is in progress. On the one hand, to show the government's determination to suppress opium, and on the other hand, to show the public's will to resist drugs. Anti-drug organizations across the country have decided to hold commemorations on this day and have been sending requests to the China National Anti-Opium Association in this city for a large number of June 3rd Memorial propaganda materials. The city has decided to hold a memorial meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 10:00 AM on June 3rd, and commemorative special issues will be published in major newspapers on that day. The materials for this special issue are jointly compiled by the City Party Department, the Municipal Government, and the Anti-Opium Association. The content focuses on drug situation investigations and the actual situation of opium suppression. It is also learned that the preparatory committee has sent propaganda outlines, oath forms, slogans, etc., to party departments, agencies, and schools in various districts to hold separate commemorations. Those who need them can send a letter to the China National Anti-Opium Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. The association believes that the relationship between opium suppression and the police is extremely close, and has sent a separate letter to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, requesting that the propaganda materials sent by the association be distributed to each district, ordering the police in each district to swear to resist drugs and requesting the director of the bureau to report on the state of opium suppression in Shanghai over the past year at the June 3rd conference. The China National Anti-Opium Association, in order to promote opium cessation, will, during the June 3rd period, introduce opium addicts who register with the association to appropriate hospitals for free or reduced-fee opium cessation. It has also been found that the Anti-Opium Association has formulated memorial measures for the June 3rd Memorial and distributed them to anti-drug organizations across the country, which are recorded as follows: (1) Memorial Conference: On this day, anti-drug organizations should jointly hold a memorial conference with local party and government agencies, public organizations, and schools in public places, read Lin Zexu's will against drugs, report on the main points of the memorial, and invite celebrities to speak on Lin Zexu's history of drug suppression. (2) Publication of Memorial Special Issues: Local publications should be contacted in advance to publish a special issue on Lin Zexu on June 3rd. (3) Public Speeches: Anti-drug comrades, schools, and public organizations should be organized into lecture teams to go to local bustling markets, streets, and open-air lectures. (4) Parades and Propaganda to Promote Popularity (5) Artistic Propaganda: Local national anti-opium associations and anti-drug propaganda associations should consult with local schools, theater companies, and entertainment venues in advance to perform anti-drug dramas, show anti-drug films, anti-drug lantern slides, and other anti-drug performances on this day. (6) Burning of Drugs: The local court should be requested in advance to present the destroyed drugs on the memorial day for burning to show determination. (7) Holding Anti-Drug Oath: Anti-drug oath forms should be widely distributed on this day to encourage people to fill them out and swear to resist drugs in order to solicit comrades. (8) Widely Post Pictures and Slogans: Lin Gong's memorial pictures and various anti-drug pictures and slogans should be prepared and widely posted everywhere for universal coverage. (9) Promote Anti-Drug Monthly: Local anti-drug organizations should sell anti-drug monthly magazines as much as possible on this day to promote anti-drug propaganda widely. (10) Fundraising for the Construction of Lin Zexu Memorial Hall: Follow the China National Anti-Opium Association's methods for fundraising for the construction of Lin Zexu Memorial Hall, publicize widely, and raise funds.

There is a Deeper Channel North of Tongsha 125

The Patrol Engineering Department Will Set Up Buoys

According to the Continental News, in order to seek separate navigation channels for incoming and outgoing ships, the Customs Patrol Engineering Department has newly measured a deeper channel north of Tongsha in the south channel of the Yangtze River estuary, which is about two feet deeper than the current navigable south channel. Buoys will be installed on the 25th of this month to facilitate navigation. In the future, a light buoy with a black body marked with the letter "A" will be installed on the left side of the new channel entrance, and a red buoy marked with the letter "B" will be installed on the right side to guide ships entering the port to navigate through the new channel.

British Nationals Hold Celebrations

The Police Will Clear Traffic

According to the Continental News, Wednesday is the birthday of King George V of England. Shanghai Municipal Council

Chinese Members Should be Added to the Land Committee 129

A Matter of Changing the Yangjingbang Regulations

Taxpayers Ask the Government to Negotiate

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association has telegraphed Foreign Minister Wang Rutang and Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun on the 28th of last month regarding the matter of adding two or three Chinese members to the Land Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council for the Public Concession. The telegram reads: "To His Excellency Wang Rutang, Foreign Minister of the Nanjing National Government, and His Excellency Zhang Yuejun, Mayor of Shanghai: The association believes that the Land Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council for the Public Concession has only three foreign members and no Chinese members. There are often differences and feelings of unfairness in land valuation and public collection. In order to seek fair treatment, the council has sent a letter to the Municipal Council requesting that two or three Chinese be added as members of the committee. The council replied that after considering the proposal to appoint two or three Chinese as members of the Land Committee, the board's proposition can only conform to what is stipulated in Article 6 of the Land Regulations. If it is desired to increase the number of land committee members, it is necessary to amend the Land Regulations, and the amendment of the Land Regulations must be negotiated by various countries and the Chinese government. The council believes that no changes should be made until the full report of Judge Fetham is completed. Upon investigation, the establishment of the Land Committee's members is indeed stipulated in the Yangjingbang Land Regulations, and the addition of Chinese members would be a change to these regulations. As for the council's statement that no changes should be made until the full report of Judge Fetham is completed, regardless of whether this is a form of procrastination, the applicability of Judge Fetham's report is still in question. The association believes that the addition of Chinese directors to the Municipal Council is also a change to the Land Regulations, which can only be achieved through negotiations between our government and the countries involved. The association believes that before the concession is taken back, it should be requested that Your Excellency promptly negotiate to add two or three Chinese members to the Land Committee of the Municipal Council. Respectfully, Wang Xiaolai and Xu Jiqing, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association, bow in respect."

Reorganization of the Overseas Chinese Federation 130

The Central Government Dispatches Fang Zizhen, Chen Chunan, and Qiu Wenshao to be Responsible

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission presented to the Central Government last year that the Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China was implying the name of the Commission and requested the Central Government to dissolve it. After learning the situation, the Central Government ordered the Shanghai Municipal Government to execute it. It is now learned that the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has already presented to the Central Government and approved the dispatch of Fang Zizhen, Chen Chunan, Qiu Wenshao, and others to Shanghai to reorganize the Overseas Chinese Federation. The reporter of the Guowen News Agency learned the following news from various parties yesterday:

History of the Overseas Chinese Federation: The Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China was established on January 26th of the first year of the Republic (1912). At that time, President Sun instructed the Minister of Interior to approve the registration and issue a bronze seal, gathering the strength of overseas Chinese to provide military supplies. The association's contribution to the anti-Yuan campaign was very significant. After its establishment, it fought against the enemy party on the one hand and provided support for overseas Chinese on the other hand, such as striving for overseas Chinese political rights, negotiating the Hong Kong and Singapore maritime defense zones, the ports' life and health tragedies, and recently working to abolish unequal treaties, protesting the harsh taxes in the Dutch East Indies, requesting the maintenance of domestic and foreign postal bureaus, requesting a reduction in overseas Chinese remittance fees, opposing the movement, and requesting amendments to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' passport law, etc. Overseas Chinese have indeed benefited greatly. Last year, the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission suddenly claimed that the name of the Overseas Chinese Federation was the same and received accusations from unknown persons that it was defrauding people, so it presented a request to the Central Government to dissolve it.

Dispatching Personnel to Shanghai to Reorganize: After learning the situation, the Central Government repeatedly investigated whether the Overseas Chinese Federation was implying a name and defrauding people, and ordered the Shanghai Municipal Government to thoroughly investigate. The Overseas Chinese Federation published an advertisement to find the accuser, but it is said that no evidence has been obtained to date. Xu Jigong, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Federation, expressed passivity due to the recurrence of old illnesses. Standing Committee members Lin Youwang and others went to Beijing several times to request a thorough investigation and request the dispatch of personnel to take over. It is now learned that the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has dispatched Fang Zizhen, Qiu Wenshao, Chen Chunan, and others as reorganizers, who have already arrived in Shanghai. Chen and Qiu are both members of the Overseas Chinese Federation.

Fang Zizhen's Speech: Yesterday, the reporter visited Fang Zizhen and Qiu Wenshao at their residence. According to their conversation, the past and present work of the Overseas Chinese Federation has indeed been an organization to fight for the interests of overseas Chinese. The Central Government's instruction to dissolve the association has made overseas Chinese extremely shocked, and we must strive to ensure that the group created by Sun Yat-sen is not dissolved at will. Now the Central Government has decided to reorganize it. The reporter also asked Fang and others about the reorganization measures, but they replied that they had not yet drafted specific measures.

Xu Jigong's Speech: The reporter then went to the residence of Xu Jigong, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Federation. According to his conversation, he has been exhausted by handling social public undertakings in recent years, and his foot disease has recurred. Whether the Overseas Chinese Federation is reorganized or dissolved, all members of the association deeply hope that the Central Government can resolve the accusations against the association as soon as possible. Mr. Jigong personally prays for this.

Export Goods

Generally Collect According to the New Tariff 132

Old Contracts Cannot Be Changed

The new export tariff came into effect yesterday. Various export industries in this city had signed contracts for exports after June 1 before the announcement of the new export tariff, and they wanted to register with the customs and still collect according to the old tariff. They inquired with Jianghai Customs and learned that the Ministry of Finance had received a telegram from the Tianjin China International Trade Chamber of Commerce requesting adoption, but the ministry replied that the export tariff has now been promulgated by clear order and is stipulated to take effect from June 1, giving a considerable period of hesitation. All domestic goods shipped overseas from June 1 should be collected according to the new export tariff to comply with the law. The request to allow merchants to register with the customs and collect according to the old tariff is difficult to approve, the telegram replied. The city will also handle the matter in the same way.

Coal Transportation Dispute on the Jiaoji Railway 133

A Conversation with Railway Officials

Coal merchants along the Jiaoji Railway had sent representatives to the Ministry of Railways to request exemption from the 20% increase in coal transportation prices ordered by the Central Government, but they did not achieve their goal and went on strike on May 21. Recently, an important official of the railway passed through Shanghai and told visitors that this time, all railways across the country increased passenger and freight rates, and the Jiaoji Railway Bureau also increased rates by 20% from May 1 in accordance with the ministry's order. For more than ten days since implementation, coal merchants in the Kunbo area suddenly went on strike. Previously, coal merchants in Kunbo, believing that the increase in freight rates was related to their business, had sent representatives to the railway bureau to request cancellation. The railway bureau replied that the price increase was not initiated by the railway bureau but was decided by the Executive Yuan of the Central Government and implemented by the Ministry of Railways. Therefore, it could not eliminate the price increase before receiving orders. The representatives believed that the increased burden was unacceptable. After repeated consultations, the railway bureau proposed a reconciliation plan, planning to reduce the price of domestic and export coal by 20% from June in the name of summer price reduction. The representatives replied to the coal merchants that the method was not thorough and still agreed to strike from May 21 for reasons of increased burden and unbearable losses. Since the Jiaoji Railway's coal freight rates were revised on November 1 of last year, the export freight rates have not been increased, and the domestic freight rates along the line have been reduced by a lot, some by as much as 40%. Now, although the price has increased by 20%, it is still lower than the old price except for a part of the export. The coal merchants' so-called losses do not seem to have a real basis. If it is said that the increase in export prices is significant, the railway bureau has also agreed to reduce the price uniformly for four months to reconcile it. Merchants can ship their contracted coal during this period. Instead, they agreed to strike, which is very harmful to the coal industry itself and the people's livelihood in Shandong Province, and is not adopted by informed people.

Measures for Collecting Export Tax on Yarn Market 134

The Chinese Cotton Mill Federation previously stated that in Category 4, Item 195 of the export tariff promulgated by the Central Government, cotton yarn is taxed at $1.12 per picul, and in Item 195-2, cotton cloth is taxed at $1.15 per picul. They did not know whether this tax refers to trade from this port to another within the country or exports overseas. If it is said to be exports overseas, the consolidated tax on exported yarn and cloth is refunded in full to encourage exports. The export tax should be exempted. If it is said to be from this port to another within the country, according to the cotton yarn consolidated tax regulations, yarn and cloth that have completed the consolidated tax are exempt from all other taxes, which is inconsistent. They sent a letter to the Consolidated Tax Office for explanation. The association received a reply from the Consolidated Tax Office yesterday stating that the matter had been consulted with Director Zhang of the Customs Office, who replied that the collection or exemption of customs duties on cotton yarn and cotton cloth declared for export overseas is still handled in accordance with the old regulations. As for the domestic transport from this port to another, if it is transported to an area that has implemented the consolidated tax, the export customs duty should be exempted. However, if it is transported to an area that has not implemented the consolidated tax, the export customs duty must still be collected in accordance with the old regulations. The corresponding letter is replied to so that all customs offices can be informed.

The Tobacco Industry Requests a Reduction in Export Tax 135

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday presented a document to the National Government's Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry stating: "On the 29th of this month, the Tobacco Industry Association of this city sent a letter stating that they had read the newly promulgated and amended export tariff of the National Government, which taxes tobacco at 7.5% of its value, requiring a tax of 1 tael and 7 mace per picul. The import tax on tobacco has caused a major blow to the domestic tobacco industry, and the export quantity has decreased sharply. If China's export tax is increased by more than ten times, domestic tobacco will not be able to be sold abroad, and the national economy and people's livelihood will be harmed. How can this be in line with the National Government's intention to promote domestic goods and develop foreign trade? The association feels deeply affected and has witnessed the decline in sales of domestic tobacco abroad in recent years. Therefore, we sincerely request your association to promptly forward the matter to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government and request that the tax rate for tobacco in the newly promulgated and amended export tariff be appropriately reduced. Upon investigation by the association, the increase from 1 mace and 5 fen to 1 tael and 7 mace this time is a unique increase. In recent years, countries such as Egypt have repeatedly increased heavy taxes on tobacco exported from our country, which has been reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiation. If the domestic export tax is increased by more than ten times, the industry's domestic and foreign transportation will inevitably not be able to sustain itself. Moreover, companies such as British American Tobacco Company have repeatedly encouraged people in provinces such as Shandong and Henan to plant tobacco and sell the remaining raw materials from tobacco factories for export, which is of some benefit to people's livelihoods. This is different from the situation of cotton, which is necessary for yarn and cloth and should be heavily taxed to reduce exports. The association's request for an appropriate reduction is for the purpose of alleviating commercial difficulties. It is reasonable to present this telegram for your review and approval. It is truly for the public good. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce bows in respect."

The Cotton Cloth Industry Firmly Refuses to Pay Dockage Fees on Behalf of Customers 136

A Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce States the Reasons

The cotton cloth customs declaration industry has been in a dispute over the payment of dockage fees on behalf of customers. After the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened a high-profile mediation between the three parties, there was still no concrete solution. The Cotton Cloth Industry Association yesterday stated its reasons to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for not being able to pay on behalf of customers, saying: "Respectfully, regarding the dockage fee case, the responsibility for payment has been admitted by the customer representatives on the spot, so there is naturally no problem. The only unresolved dispute is which party should pay on behalf of the customers. After careful consideration by this association, we are unable to agree. We respectfully submit this to your association. The dockage fee must be paid when the goods are exported, and customs practice has always been to collect it from the customs declaration firm that undertakes the shipment. Therefore, in terms of facts and procedures, it is indispensable for the customs declaration industry to pay on behalf of customers. For our industry, we want to pay on behalf of customers but cannot. Therefore, it is only reasonable that this obligation should be carried out by the customs declaration industry on behalf of customers. However, the customer representatives expressed a rather strong intention on that day to force our industry to undertake the task, abandoning the direct path and taking a roundabout route. The true motive is self-evident. If it is as they say, the following reversals will inevitably occur: (1) After the customs declaration industry pays the customs on behalf of the customers, they do not directly seek compensation from the customers but indirectly collect it from our industry. (2) The customers who bear the responsibility for payment do not directly hand over the payment to the customs declaration firm that has already paid on their behalf but indirectly hand it over to our industry, which has no connection. (3) Our industry first collects from the customers and then pays to the customs declaration firm. We are originally a completely unrelated third party, but we must be forced to assume the obligation of intermediate transfer. (4) Many customers operate their own customs declaration firms. They do not compensate their own firms but hand over the payment to other firms, blaming others instead of themselves. Nothing in the world is more ridiculous than this. Moreover, our industry has an upstream and downstream relationship with the customers. If it were not absolutely necessary, why would we be willing to damage the relationship? For example, although the Social Affairs Bureau has announced that each customer should attach an additional 3 mace and 4 fen of silver to the consolidated tax to be handed over to our industry for collection and settlement, even though it has been more than a month now, our industry has still been unable to collect it from the customers as required. However, we cannot but pay the customs declaration workers in full. The previous example can serve as a warning, and we fear repeating the same mistake. After our industry has declined, we can no longer afford to increase the burden. Therefore, we express our difficulties and sincerely request your association to examine and verify the facts, uphold justice, and resolve the matter fairly. We are extremely grateful."

Uniform Price for Kerosene for Both Chinese and Foreign Businesses 137

The Ministry of Railways sent a letter to the municipal government yesterday regarding equal treatment in kerosene transportation prices for Chinese and foreign businesses. It reads: "Respectfully, after reviewing the minutes of the National Commercial Transport Conference previously convened by this Ministry, and with reference to the proposal submitted by the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce on behalf of the Shanghai Guanghua Kerosene Company and the Sino-American Kerosene Company, requesting that they receive the same preferential transportation rate of 70% as the Mobil and Asiatic Petroleum Companies, a resolution was passed that all companies, Chinese or foreign, should receive equal treatment. This decision was duly recorded by the Ministry and communicated to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations for compliance. It has now been reported that the current freight car transportation regulations of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway stipulate that the special price for transporting kerosene is calculated by deducting 50% from the second-class freight rate, but this is only applicable to full carloads and only for northbound shipments. The current freight car transportation regulations of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway stipulate that kerosene transported in tank cars, boxed drums, or cans is charged at a rate that deducts 55% from the second-class full carload freight rate, regardless of whether the company or business is Chinese or foreign. There is no discrepancy in these special kerosene rates on the two lines. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's statement that the Mobil and Asiatic Petroleum Companies are charged at a rate of 70% is not accurate. We are informing your esteemed government accordingly for dissemination to avoid any misunderstanding."

Central Bank Inspection Report 142

Report Number Ninety-One

The Central Bank's ninety-first inspection report on issuance reserves reads: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Charter, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the banknotes issued by this bank. The ninety-first inspection was conducted at the bank's Issuance Bureau on May 30, 1931. The results are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total value of banknotes issued: silver dollars 33,176,350, including silver dollar banknotes 31,614,962 and subsidiary currency banknotes 1,561,388. Total value of banknote reserves: 33,176,350 silver dollars, including cash reserves of 23,416,359.60 silver dollars. This cash reserve consists of 16,208,685.85 silver dollars held in the bank's issuance vault, 2,177,832 silver dollars held in branches in various locations, and 5,029,841.75 silver dollars held with other banks. Guarantee reserves are equivalent to 9,759,990.04 silver dollars. (B) Total value of customs gold unit banknotes issued: 815,737.20 customs gold units. Total value of customs gold unit banknote reserves: 815,737.20 customs gold units. This reserve includes 13,595.61 taels of standard gold, valued at 60% customs gold units as above. In accordance with Article 2 of the Central Bank Note Exchange Regulations, cash reserves constitute 60% and guarantee reserves constitute 40%. The results of this inspection show that cash reserves exceed 60%, while guarantee reserves are less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. May 30, 1931. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun. Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiqing."

Third Strike by Bookbinding Workers 146

Insisting on a 40% Wage Increase

Approximately 1,800 workers from 150 Chinese and foreign bookbinding shops in the city, including Ma Hongji, went on strike again starting on the 30th, with authorities' attempts at persuasion proving unsuccessful. The details are as follows:

Third Strike: Chinese and foreign bookbinding workers have previously staged two strikes demanding changes to their treatment conditions. These were fully resolved after repeated mediation by the Bureau of Social Affairs, with wages uniformly increased by 10% of the original amount. All workers expressed dissatisfaction and went on strike again, gathering at the workers' union in Tianji Lane, Rue Say-Zoong Road to question the representatives. The union repeatedly tried to persuade them without success.

Workers' Congress: The bookbinding union immediately convened a general meeting of all representatives at the Third District Party Headquarters to gather opinions. Representatives from the Bureau of Social Affairs, including Wang Bing, and 116 representatives attended. The presidium, consisting of Zhang Jinhong, Zhang Haosheng, and Chao Guosheng, reported on the progress. Representatives from the Bureau of Social Affairs then provided guidance, but the workers insisted on a 40% wage increase, making it impossible to stop them. It was resolved to appoint ten people, including Lu Axiang, Shen Changjiang, Chen Zhiting, and Xue Lanxin, to assist the board of supervisors in coordinating with the Book Association to firmly demand that apprentices in the bookbinding industry be treated in accordance with the previously agreed-upon agreement.

No Regulations for Unions to Intervene in Employer-Employer Disputes 147

Bureau of Social Affairs' Reply to Lawyer Chen Zhigao's Letter

Lawyer Chen Zhigao inquired about whether the Bureau of Social Affairs has the authority to mediate and dispatch personnel to investigate disputes between employers, citing the Shuimu Industry Union and Wang Fukang Xinhasheng letters as examples. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs replied, stating: "Regarding your inquiry about whether a union has the authority to mediate and dispatch personnel to investigate disputes between employers, we have found that the Trade Union Law does not explicitly grant unions the authority to mediate disputes between employers, so they do not have such authority. This reply is hereby provided for your reference."

Significant Decline in Zhejiang Province's Spring Silkworm Harvest 148

Only 30% of the Expected Yield

The silkworm season in Hangzhou, Shaoxing, Huzhou, and Jiaxing in Zhejiang Province starts earlier than in Jiangsu Province, with Hangzhou and Shaoxing starting several days earlier than Jiaxing and Huzhou. This year, the weather has been unfavorable, with continuous spring rains. Early silkworms were found to be diseased and were abandoned, and farmers raised late silkworms as a substitute. However, the cold weather and prolonged rainy season delayed their development, resulting in a significant shortage of cocoons. Only about 30% of the expected yield was harvested. In Hangzhou's Linping, Yuhang, Pingyao, Chang'an, and Haining, as well as the old Shaoxing prefecture, cocoon merchants are only receiving about 30% of the cocoons compared to previous years. Shanghai silk merchants, noting the sharp decline in overseas silk markets and the poor silkworm season, have been reluctant to invest in Hangzhou to purchase cocoons this year. Most merchants have set up small-scale drying operations. The cocoon markets in Hangzhou and Shaoxing have been open for over a week, but the supply of cocoons is limited, with many being of inferior quality. Each merchant's purchase volume is only about 20-30% of previous years. Most have now stopped purchasing. The highest cocoon price was for improved Shaoxing cocoons, reaching 60 or 58 yuan, while the lowest price was for Hangzhou cocoons, only 40-42 yuan. The average price is around 50 yuan. Drying requires 320-330 catties of raw cocoons, while reeling requires 580-590 catties. Personnel sent by Shanghai silk mills, such as Tianchang, to Hangzhou and Shaoxing to purchase cocoons have now concluded their operations and returned to Shanghai.

Collecting Pig Inspection Fees 149

Butchers in the Concessions to Meet Today to Discuss

The pre-slaughter inspection fees for fresh pork in the city's concessions were previously contracted by Zhang Baokun, who charged one dime per pig to the government. Starting yesterday, the municipal government took over the operations itself, with personnel from the Finance and Health Bureaus charging per pig at the Xuejiabang pig market and issuing permits. Butchers in the concessions found the procedures cumbersome and time-consuming, hindering sales. Furthermore, misunderstandings arose because the previous contractor charged on a monthly basis, leading many to not purchase permits. The municipal government deemed this failure to purchase permits inappropriate and immediately seized the pigs, totaling over 2,000. Representatives of the butchers, led by Huang Xunhua, petitioned the Finance and Health Bureaus and managed to have the seized pigs temporarily released into the concessions around 5:00 PM yesterday. Butchers in the concessions are scheduled to meet at 2:00 PM this afternoon to discuss the situation.

Wang Junsheng

Diligently Handling Jiang-Zhe Burial Affairs 150

Since the winter of the Wuchen year (1928), Mr. Wang Junsheng, Director of the Pushan Villa, has been entrusted by Mr. Wang Yiting, Chairman of the Joint Charity Organization, to handle the burial of exposed skeletal remains in the Jiang-Zhe border region. He has worked diligently and tirelessly for the past three and a half years, burying a total of 40,318 exposed coffins and skeletal remains. A few days ago, he personally went to Jiaxing to discuss continued operations with local philanthropists Mr. Zheng Zanqing and Mr. Xia Bosen. Burial operations will begin on August 20th in Chiwan, Youchegang, Xinfeng, Fengqiao, Wangdian, and Sangu Temple in order to quickly bury the remains and fulfill the wishes of the deceased. Burial operations in Wujiang, Zhenze, Tongli, Lili, Luxu, and Yanmu and other areas in Suzhou Prefecture will commence after the Wujiang and Wu County Magistrates complete the procedures for the spring operations. It is also reported that there are still over 120,000 unburied skeletal remains in various parts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Mr. Wang is deeply concerned about the funding shortages for these operations. It is hoped that philanthropists will be inspired to contribute generously to this charitable cause, as its merit is immeasurable.
